"								TOP	1.3		 Andean Regional Development								"Tiwanaku (Tiahuanaco, Lake Titicaca)"	1.6		"Stone sculptural traditions of anthropomorphic stelae and low relief carvings. Cut-stone public architechture including sunken rectangular  courts and pyramidal  or stepped platform mounds. Settlement  pattern hierarchy with large urban site, secondary centres, and farmsteads with raised-field agricultural systems in highlands. Serving and ceremonial pottery including kero drinking goblets, anthropomorphic and zoomorphic vessels, polychromes typically red-slipped with motifs in black, white, orange and blue-grey. Characteristics utilitarian plain-ware pottery. Camelid wool and cotton textiles including polychrome striped warp-faced plain weaves and figural tunics of interlocked tapestry technique, both with loop stitch embroidery. Bronze, gold and silver metallurgy, diverse lithic and lapidary industries. Follows the Andean Regional Development tradition, precedes the Aymara Kingdoms and Andean Regional States traditions. In the terminology of the Tiawanaku region, the tradition includes the terminal ""Early Intermediate Period"" and the ""Middle Horizon"" and precedes the ""Late Intermediate Period"". This partly overlaps with the Andean Regional Development."								 Andean Regional Development	2.2		"Localised but interacting states with complex ideology, symbol systems, and social forms. Highly developed ceramics, metallurgy, and weaving. Follows the end of the Upper Formative manifestation; in the northern and central highlands, after the fall of Chavin."								Highland Andean Formative	3.5		"Sedentary agriculturalist with a reliance on maize and domesticated animals, living in large villages and ceremonial centres. Ranking or stratification is present, as in pottery manufacture and metallurgy. Defined by the first appearance of ceramics, this period includes the phases of Initial Period and the Early Horizon. In the northern half of the area, the Chavin state emerges midway through this phase, and there the period ends with the collapse of the Chavin; in the southern half of the area, the period ends with the beginning of the Andean Regional Development phase. "								"Highland Andean Late Archaic (Late Preceramic, Terminal Late Archaic, Late Archaic, Transitional)"	4.5		"A variety of projectile  point styles including lanceolate, foliate, and triangular forms. In the central and south-central Andes, rare ceremonial sites consisting of rectangular/ovid structures with central hearths and sometimes underground flues. Follows the Early Highland Andean Archaic tradition, and precedes the Highland Andean Formative tradition. "								Highland Andean Early Archaic	7		"Chipped-stone industry including relatively small, leaf-shaped, diamond-shaped or shouldered projectile points and unifacial tools. Industries include bone tools, rare ground stone, aand ornaments of mineral, shell, or bone. Cave occupation sites, with some open-air camps. Pictographs in a variety of pigment colours. Follows the Late Andean Hunting-Collecting tradition and precedes the Late Highland Andean Archaic tradition."								Old South American Hunting-Collecting	15		"Various kinds of bifacial and unifacial stone tool technologies, features such as hearths and small storage pits, quarry, camp and kill sites. The first cultural tradition in Andean South America; it precedes the Late Andean Hunting-Collecting tradtion."																		Andean - Coastal	block	150	246/177/182		off							TOP	0.53		 Andean Regional States (Late Intermediate Period (LIP)) and Aymara Kingdom (Lake Titicaca) 								 Andean Regional States (Late Intermediate Period (LIP))	0.9		"Stylistically highly variable. Handmade and mold-made ceramics, bronze-copper-silver-gold metallurgy, fine cotton and camelid-wool textiles, elaborate irrigation and terracing, camelid herding, some cities and fortified settlements, burial monuments. Follows the collapse of the Middle Horizon empires of Wari and Tiahuanaco, precedes the expansion of the Late Horizon Inka empire. "								TOP	1.2		"Moche (Mochica, Early Chimu)"								"Moche (Mochica, Early Chimu)"	1.95		"Ceramics with black paste and, especially, orange or red paste with bi-or trichrome (red, black, white) painting or with decoration in relief, produced by molding, stamping or surface additions. Ornaments of gold, silver, copper, or alloys, manufactured by a variety of methods including lost wax casting. Camelid wool or textiles with polychrome decoration made on rudimentary looms. Wattle-and-daub or adobe houses with packed earthen floors. Monumental public architechture, called huacas, built out of adobe and consisting of platforms, terraces, and ramps. Polychrome murals. Follows the Andean Regional Development tradition and precedes the Wari tradition. Encompasses the last six centuries of the Early Intermediate period and the first two centuries of the Middle Horizon. "								Coastal Andean Late Formative (Early Horizon)	2.2		TOP								Coastal Andean Late Formative (Early Horizon)	3		"Pottery on the north coast varies in thickness and is often decorated with incision, stamped circle and dots, textile and netimpressions, or occasional painting. South coast pottery has incised designs associated with postfired polychrome  painting as well as simpler prefired painting. Vessel shapes on the north coast include tall-neck bottles, thick stirrup spout vessels, neckless ollas, tall-neck and short-necked jars, large jars with everted rims, and open bowls, whereas the south coast vessel shapes are dominated by double-spout-and bridge vessels and open bowls. Long, thin ground-slate projectile points are typical of the north coast. Woven cotton textiles with geometric designs occur on the north coast, whwere as elaborate embroidered  wool and cotton textiles typify the south coast. Copper and gold artefacts appear for the first time in this period. Houses are rectangular and irregular quandrangular structures with stone footings and cane and/or wooden superstructures, and most are laid out in an irregular pattern. Settlement patterns are characterised by large communities of interconnected room complexes that incorporate low platforms.  Follows the Early Coastal Andean Formative tradition, precedes the Andean Reagional Developmental tradition. "								Coastal Andean Early Formative	4.1		"Pottery is relatively thing and unevenly fired, with principal forms being neckless ollas, short-necked jars, and open bowls. Some thin-walled stirrup-spout vessels occur in sites along the north coast. Twined and woven cotton textiles are present. Sites are dominated by very large bilaterally symmetrical flat-topped  mounds associated with rectangular and circular plazas. Medium-sized stone mounds are often present and laid out in precisely aligned rows. Follows the Late Coastal Andean Archaic tradition and precedes the Late Coastal Andean Formative tradition. "								Coastal  Andean Early Archaic	7		Agricultural coastal villages define the Coastal Andean Archaic. The absence of ceramics is also a key diagnostic feature. Follows the Late Andean Hunting-Collecting tradition and precedes the Early Coastal Andean Formative tradition. 																		Andean - Northern	block	150	246/177/182		off							TOP	0.48		Chimu								Chimu	1.05		"Finely burnished black-ware ceramics including stirrup-sprout vessels with surface treatments such as panels of raised strippling or repeated waves, appliqued animal, human, and mythic figures. Moldmade adobes used to construct rectilinear compounds enclosing erchitectural features such as baffled entries, ramps and benches, and niches; interior walls decorated with sculpted reliefs depicting waves, fish, pelicans, and other marine motifs. Settlement patterns vary, but may range from large urban centers to small rural hamlets. Follows the Moche tradition and precedes the Inka tradition. "								Huari (or Wari)	1.2		"Pottery, artitecture, textiles, carved stone, carved wood, carved bone, feather work, sculpted stone statuary, and metal ornaments. Planned orthogonal architectural buildings with corbeled floor supports, niches, corridors, galleries, open courtyards, drainage canals, and open plazas, as well as specialised irregular buildings such as D-shaped ceremonial structures. Follows the Andean Regional Development tradition, precedes the Andean Regional States tradition. "								TOP	1.3		Nazca (Nasca)								Nazca (Nasca)	2.2		"Polychrome potterypainted in up to fifteen colours with complex mythical as well as naturalistic motifs; evidence of warfare and the ritual use of human trophy heads; large ground drawings (geoglyphs) etched on the surface of the desert in the form of lines, geometric forms, and naturalistic figures; settlements small to moderate in size, constructed of irregular fieldstone or adobe; cermonial centers consisting of modified natural hills forming pyramidal structures. Precedes the huari tradition and follows the Late Coastal Andean Formative tradition. Corresponds to the Early Intermediate Period in the Peruvian chronological sequence; follows the Early horizon Paracas culture and precedes the Middle Horizon Huari (Wari) culture. "								Chavin	2.8		"Monumental stone and adobe temple with plazas. Stone and adobe  sculpture, painted textiles, metalwork, and decorated pottery expressing religious ideology through a complex symbolic system. There frequently depict a paramount supernatural and secondarydeities. Ceramics are typically fired black, polished, and embellished with standardised sets of incised, stamped, textured, and molded design elements and motifs. Abundant exotic pottery, shells, and precious stones are often found in both ritual and domestic contexts. Overlaps with the Highland Andean Formative tradition and precedes the Andean Regional Development period. Corresponds to the Early Horizon, which follows the Initial Period and proceedds the Early Intermediate Period."																		Andean - Southern	block	150	246/177/182		off							TOP	0.5		South Andean Ceramic								South Andean Ceramic	2.5		"Agricultural villages with ceramics. Strongly influenced by the Incas. Follows the Highland Andean Formative, precedes the historic period. "																		Andean - Amazon	block	150	246/177/182		off							TOP	0.15		Tupi								Tupi	1.5		"For both the Guarani and the Tupinamba, a sand-tempered pottery sometimes decorated by elaborate polychrome painting in red and/or black or brown on a white slip. In the case of the Guarani, the coiled technique of vessel forming has not been often obliterated externally (corrugated), whereas the Tupinamba it has been smoothed; moreover, vessels forms are completely different in the two subtraditions. Decorated techinques include nail incisions. Lithic intruments are small, pollish stone axeheads; stone pendants; quartz T-shaped labrets; bipolar flaked chert tools and massive bifaced choppers. Wooden houses were elongated or rounded and often arranged linearly or in a circle around a plaza. c. 1500-150 B.P. Tupian languages were spoken from 5000 B.P. to the present. Carbon-14 date the archaeology Tupi ceramics (Guarani and Tupinamba) from 1800-300B.P. Tupi ethnocentric cultures were known from 450B.P. to the present. "																		Argentina intervals	block	150	246/187/182		off							TOP	0.5										Late Parana-Pampean	1.5		"The presence of ceramics is the primary diagnostic feature of this tradition. Small, triangular projectile points are also diagnostic. Follows the Early Parana-Pampean tradition and precedes the historic period. "								Early Parana-Pampean	7		Distinctive triangular stemmed projectile points. Follows the Late Andean Hunting-Collecting tradition and includes the initial colonization of some parts of the Parana-Pampean tradition. 																		Argentina - Patagonian Coast	block	150	246/187/182		off							TOP	0.05		Magellan-Fuegan								Magellan-Fuegan	6.3		"Bark or plank caones. Two types of dwellings: dome-shaped huts of branches and leaves, and conical huts of poles. Bone tools arevery abundant  but do not outnumber the lithic ones. Most diagnostics are two harpoon classes, detachable point with one or two bards and fix-to-handle multiple barbed ones. Lithic tools are very abundant, little varied and, except for the weapon points, they were poor specialised in function. This is the only native cultural tradition definable in the area, although there is an earlier record of the occasional presence of small groups of another, stil culturally undetermined, tradition."																		Amazon - main intervals	block	150	246/187/182		off							TOP	0.05		Late Amazonian								Late Amazonian	2		"Sedentary and possibly socially ranked mixed horticulturalists and intensive agriculturalists living in large villages often placed on mounds. Some cultures also have representative mounds. Subsistence ranges from possible manioc cultivation to be intensive maize cultivation late in the period. Fishing is the most important source of faunal food, but late prehistoric period people have stable isotope ratios that suggest a dominance of maize in their protein supply. People made elaborately decorated pottery and sculptures and often buried their dead in urns in large cemeteries used for long periods. The characteristic polychrome subtradition pottery bears elaborate polychrome and/or incised and modeled decoration. The forms include adorno bowls, effigies of many kinds, anthropomorphic zoomorphic  burial urns, female rattle figurines, and pendant pigment pots, stools, etc. The Incised and Punctate subtradition pottery corpus also includes adorno bowls, diverse effigies, burial bowls, female figurine rattles, but in addition has large statues of effigy vessels representing realistic human images. Follows the Early Amazonian tradition and continues into the historic period."								Early Amazonian	7		"At least partly sedentary villagers relying mainly on fishing and shellfishing supplemented with plant collection, hunting, and probably plant cultivation. By the end of the tradition. The pottery tradition begins with simple pottery bowls and ends with more varied pottery. Deposits of the Pottery Archaic subtradition was first identified in excavations in large shell midden sites along the mainstream Amazon and its estuary in the lower Amazon of the Brazil and the coastal plain of the Guianas. Most of the pottery sherds found in the earliest sites are from plain sand-tempered bowls. Only a few sherds at each site were decorated , with red paint, incision or corrugation, depending on the site. Some pottery at some of the later sites of the tradition is shell tempered, but grit or sand temper continues to be more common. About 3% of sherds are decorated with repeated geometric grooved designs. Later, Formative subtradition sites have more elaborate pottery with broadline incision, zone incised hatched, red and white paint, modeling, adorno bowls, and animal effigy vessels. Some of these Formative subtradition sites have griddles; other have decorative stamps and tabacco effigy pipes. The most common figurative images are zoomorphic, but there are rare anthropomorphic animals too. Grit-tempered is common, but sherd temper was characteristic of teh sites on Marajo island at the south of the Amazon. Bone and shell were made into tools, such as scrapers and simple figurative carvings. Some sites have crude flaked lithics, others not. Follows the Old Amazonian Collecting-Hunting tradition, precedes the Late Amazonian tradition. "								Old Amazonian Collecting-Hunting	11		"Nomadic collector hunters with a focus on tropical forest nuts and fruits, fish, shellfish, and smaller game. These people were rock artists and makers of a wide variety of flaked-stone tools. The Palaeoindian subtradition was first recongnised in surface finds of finely flaked triangular stemmed or hollow-based projectile points of hyaline quartz or chalcedony. When finally excavated, the projectile points were found with a variety of other tools, including unifacial gravers, slug-shaped scrapers (limaces), blades, and flake scrapers. Larger, coarser tools with fewer flake removals were made of quartz breccia. The Palaeoindian subtradition is similar to the earliest accepted Palaeoindian cultureof central and southern Brazil, first described at Lagoa Santa, Minas Gerais state, and of the Iaparica culture of Goias. The Archaic tradition is characterised by percussion-flaked hayaline quartz lithics lacking bifacial projectile points. Begins the known human occupation of the Amazon; precedes the Early Amazonian tradition. "																		Amazon - Brazillian Uplands	block	150	246/187/182		off							TOP	0.05		Late East Brazilian Uplands								Late East Brazilian Uplands	5		"Ceramics are present. Many sites show evidence of horticulture, in particular, manioc. Most sites have bola stones and plugs. Follows the Early Brazilian Uplands tradition, precedes the historic period. "								Early East Brazilian Uplands	11		"Most Early East Brazilian Uplands sites occur in rock shelters, although open sites exist. Projectile points are made from bone and stone. Stone points tend to have contracting stems and square or slightly hooked shoulders. Not all sites, however, have projectile points. Long and narrow stone scrapers are more common, and some sites have large, hooked stone knives. A few Early East Brazilian Upland sites have bola stones, a trait common with the prehistoric cultures in the Pampas region to the south. Polished and grooved axes are also present. Although most sites have the remainsof modern fauna, several of the sites in the states of Mina Gerais and Bahia contain bones of extinct Pleistocene megafauna as well as modern fauna. Follows the Late Palaeoindian tradition, precedes the Late East Brazilian Uplands tradition. "																		Amazon - Brazillian Lowlands	block	150	246/187/182		off	"Location: The entire length of the Brazilian coastal plain south of the mouth of the Amazonian river. Important sites: Pantano do Sul, Praia da Tapera, Sambaqui da Caiera, Sambaqui de Camboinhas, Sambaqui da carnica, Sambaqui at Forte Marechal Luz, Sambaqui da Pedra Oca, Sambaqui da Picaguera, Sambaquis de Ponta das Almas, Sambaqui do Rio Sao Joao. "						TOP	0.65		Sambaqui								Sambaqui	7		"The major diagnostic trait is the presence of shell mounds. These mounds consist consist of mollusk shell mixed with windblown and water-born deposits. Some mounds are refuse mounds, and others serve as platforms for habitation structures. Burials may occur in both types of mounds. Also diagnostic are bone and shell fishhooks and an economy based on mullusks, wild nuts and fruit. Overlaps the Early east Brasilian Uplands and the Late East Brasilian Uplands traditions in coastal areas, precedes the historic. "																																								Ice-Rafting Events in N.Atlantic (coolings)	event	70	236/204/215								EVENT												1.4 ka	1.4										2.8 ka	2.8										4.2 ka	4.2										5.9 ka	5.9										8.2 ka	8.1										9.4 ka	9.4										10.3 ka	10.3										11.1 ka	11.1										H1	16.5										H2	23.5										H3	32										H4	39.5										H5	47										H6	67										H7?	87																																										Greenland NGRIP Oxy-18 (b2k)	point	250			off	"From Seierstad et al.
